<div id="review_1669832473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1669832473" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35695870-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432820959p2/35695870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1669832473?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/35695870-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545389853" href="/book/show/11317810-wonder-struck">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1669832473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10682261432018114310">There is such a good book. There are two stories going on at once; One is written through pictures, the other through words. It bounces between the two. <br/> <br/>In one story, the one conveyed through words, we have a boy trying to figure out where he belongs after the death of his mother. In the beginning of the story he is deaf in one ear, after an accident he loses all of his hearing. One night while going through his mother's belongings he finds a clue to the identity of his father. He follows this </span>
  <span id="freeText10682261432018114310" style="display:none">There is such a good book. There are two stories going on at once; One is written through pictures, the other through words. It bounces between the two. <br /> <br />In one story, the one conveyed through words, we have a boy trying to figure out where he belongs after the death of his mother. In the beginning of the story he is deaf in one ear, after an accident he loses all of his hearing. One night while going through his mother's belongings he finds a clue to the identity of his father. He follows this clue to New York.<br /> <br />In the picture story we have an ealier time setting than the other story. We have a deaf girl unhappy with her life. She spends all of her time locked away in her father's house. Her family feels it is too dangerous for her to verture out into the world. She sneaks away to the city, New York. <br /> <br />This is over 600 pages, but it does not take a very long time to read. Well over half of the book is comprised of page sized illustrations. I fell in love with the way this story was put together. I have never seen another book like this. I would so read more books put together in the same fashion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10682261432018114310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_343865274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343865274" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343865274?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">the young at heart of every age</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=children-literature">children-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343865274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2315789506691882415">In <i>Wonderstruck</i>, Brian Selznick returns to the groundbreaking combination of text and pencil drawings that made <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret' title='The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a> such a — well, wonder. <br/><br/>With Selznick’s work, it is much too easy to reveal too much and spoil the magic. So I will limit myself to saying that the adventures of Ben Wilson and Rose Mayhew are divided by 50 years and 1,250 miles, but the two stories — one beginning in Gunflint Lake, Minnesota, in 1977 and the other beginning in Hoboken, N.J., in 1927 — will </span>
  <span id="freeText2315789506691882415" style="display:none">In <i>Wonderstruck</i>, Brian Selznick returns to the groundbreaking combination of text and pencil drawings that made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret" title="The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a> such a — well, wonder. <br /><br />With Selznick’s work, it is much too easy to reveal too much and spoil the magic. So I will limit myself to saying that the adventures of Ben Wilson and Rose Mayhew are divided by 50 years and 1,250 miles, but the two stories — one beginning in Gunflint Lake, Minnesota, in 1977 and the other beginning in Hoboken, N.J., in 1927 — will converge at the Museum of Natural History in New York City. How these two adventures intersect will leave the readers — dare I say it? — wonder struck by Selznick’s talent in both illustrating and storytelling. <br /><br />As with <i>The Invention of Hugo Cabret, Wonderstruck</i> is a children’s book that adults will enjoy even more than the its target audience. Highly, highly recommended for young and old.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2315789506691882415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('92zMz42UQjPEzTkhstXPnit+3WasWo0bCqg68z7gczHPZ9mXw4TXurxDwiJpu8p/LrZFx9+ifYhVz8yndX3dSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jbK0d41nkNHNVZh3RQmKccE5zKXaz5HK/SokibD0nMy1uaEvw3cFWLXbY3SeZ4+QxPFUBKk3YVmiTdLd+2kytQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick">About Brian Selznick</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201028714p3/38120.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick">Brian Selznick
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,081
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14073097540072649063">Hello there. My name is Brian Selznick and I’m the author and illustrator of The Invention of Hugo Cabret. I was born in 1966 in New Jersey. I have a sister who is a teacher, a brother who is a brain surgeon, and five nephews and one niece. I studied at The Rhode Island School of Design and after I graduated from college I worked at Eeyore’s Books for Children in New York City. I learned all about</span>
  <span id="freeText14073097540072649063" style="display:none">Hello there. My name is Brian Selznick and I’m the author and illustrator of The Invention of Hugo Cabret. I was born in 1966 in New Jersey. I have a sister who is a teacher, a brother who is a brain surgeon, and five nephews and one niece. I studied at The Rhode Island School of Design and after I graduated from college I worked at Eeyore’s Books for Children in New York City. I learned all about children’s books from my boss Steve Geck who is now an editor of children’s books at Greenwillow. While I was at Eeyore’s I also painted the windows for holidays and book events. <br /><br />My first book, The Houdini Box, which I both wrote and illustrated, was published in 1991 while I was still working at the bookstore. Since then, I have illustrated many books for children, including Frindle by Andrew Clements, The Doll People by Ann Martin and Laura Godwin, Amelia and Eleanor Go for a Ride by Pam Muñoz Ryan and The Dinosaurs of Waterhouse Hawkins by Barbara Kerley, which received a 2001 Caldecott Honor.<br /><br />I have also written a few other books myself, including The Boy of a Thousand Faces, but The Invention of Hugo Cabret is by far the longest and most involved book I’ve ever worked on. <br /><br />I live in Brooklyn, New York, and San Diego, California.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14073097540072649063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
